				<div class="minerva__subtitle"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">&#160;&#160;(Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Starbucks_Corp.&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="Starbucks Corp.">Starbucks Corp.</a>)</span></div>

			<div id="bodyContent" class="content"><div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="mw-parser-output"><section class="mf-section-0" id="mf-section-0"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about the worldwide coffee chain. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Starbucks_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Starbucks (disambiguation)">Starbucks (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>

<p><b>Starbucks Corporation</b> is an American <a href="/wiki/Coffee" title="Coffee">coffee</a> company and <a href="/wiki/List_of_coffeehouse_chains" title="List of coffeehouse chains">coffeehouse chain</a>. Starbucks was founded in <a href="/wiki/Seattle" title="Seattle">Seattle</a>, Washington, in 1971. As of early 2019, the company operates over 30,000 locations worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> Starbucks has been described as the main representative of "second wave coffee," a retrospectively termed movement that popularized artisanal coffee, particularly darkly roasted coffee.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> Since the 2000s, <a href="/wiki/Third_wave_of_coffee" title="Third wave of coffee">third wave coffee</a> makers have targeted quality-minded coffee drinkers with hand-made coffee based on lighter roasts, while Starbucks nowadays uses automated espresso machines for efficiency and safety reasons.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:0_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-8">[8]</a></sup></p><table class="infobox <li><a href="/wiki/Torrefazione_Italia" title="Torrefazione Italia">Torrefazione Italia</a></li></ul></div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;">Website</th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://Starbucks.com">starbucks<wbr></wbr>.com</a></span></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;line-height: 1.35em;"><b>Footnotes / references</b><br><sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-loxcel_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loxcel-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SEC2017_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SEC2017-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table><p>Starbucks locations serve hot and cold drinks, whole-bean coffee, microground instant coffee known as VIA, <a href="/wiki/Espresso" title="Espresso">espresso</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caffe_latte" class="mw-redirect" title="Caffe latte">caffe latte</a>, full- and loose-leaf <a href="/wiki/Tea" title="Tea">teas</a> including <a href="/wiki/Teavana" title="Teavana">Teavana</a> tea products,<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> Evolution Fresh juices, <a href="/wiki/Frappuccino" title="Frappuccino">Frappuccino</a> beverages, <a href="/wiki/Pascal_Rigo" title="Pascal Rigo">La Boulange</a> <a href="/wiki/Pastries" class="mw-redirect" title="Pastries">pastries</a>, and snacks including items such as chips and crackers; some offerings (including their annual fall launch of the <a href="/wiki/Pumpkin_Spice_Latte" title="Pumpkin Spice Latte">Pumpkin Spice Latte</a>) are seasonal or specific to the locality of the store. Many stores sell pre-packaged food items, hot and cold sandwiches, and drinkware including mugs and <a href="/wiki/Whiskey_tumbler" class="mw-redirect" title="Whiskey tumbler">tumblers</a>; select "Starbucks Evenings" locations offer <a href="/wiki/Beer" title="Beer">beer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wine" title="Wine">wine</a>, and appetizers.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Starbucks-brand coffee, ice cream, and bottled cold coffee drinks are also sold at <a href="/wiki/Grocery_stores" class="mw-redirect" title="Grocery stores">grocery stores</a>.
</p><p>Starbucks first became profitable in <a href="/wiki/Coffee_in_Seattle" title="Coffee in Seattle">Seattle</a> in the early 1980s.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> Despite an initial economic downturn with its expansion into the <a href="/wiki/Midwestern_United_States" title="Midwestern United States">Midwest</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia" title="British Columbia">British Columbia</a> in the late 1980s,<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> the company experienced revitalized prosperity with its entry into <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a> in the early 1990s through a series of <a href="/wiki/Coffee_wars" title="Coffee wars">coffee wars</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> The first Starbucks location outside North America opened in <a href="/wiki/Tokyo" title="Tokyo">Tokyo</a> in 1996; overseas properties now constitute almost one-third of its stores.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> The company opened an average of two new locations daily between 1987 and 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> In 2010, the company began its <a href="/wiki/Starbucks_Reserve" title="Starbucks Reserve">Starbucks Reserve</a> program for single-origin coffees and high-end coffee shops. Starbucks operates six roasteries with tasting rooms and 43 coffee bars as part of the program.<sup id="cite_ref-Seattle_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Seattle-16">[16]</a></sup> In November 2019, the world's largest Starbucks opened in <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Magnificent_Mile" title="Magnificent Mile">Magnificent Mile</a> as the sixth roastery location.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p><p>On December 1, 2016, <a href="/wiki/Howard_Schultz" title="Howard Schultz">Howard Schultz</a> announced he would resign as <a href="/wiki/CEO" class="mw-redirect" title="CEO">CEO</a> effective April 2017 and would be replaced by <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Johnson_(executive)" title="Kevin Johnson (executive)">Kevin Johnson</a>. Johnson assumed the role of CEO on April 3, 2017,<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> and Howard Schultz retired to become Chairman Emeritus effective June 26, 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>

</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(1)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2><section class="mf-section-1 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-1">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pike_Place_Market_-_Starbucks_circa_1977A.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Pike_Place_Market_-_Starbucks_circa_1977A.jpg/220px-Pike_Place_Market_-_Starbucks_circa_1977A.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="815"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 149px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Pike_Place_Market_-_Starbucks_circa_1977A.jpg/220px-Pike_Place_Market_-_Starbucks_circa_1977A.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="149" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pike_Place_Market_-_Starbucks_circa_1977A.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Interior of the <a href="/wiki/Pike_Place_Market" title="Pike Place Market">Pike Place Market</a> location in 1977</div></div></div>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Founding">Founding</span></h3>
<p>The first Starbucks was opened in Seattle, Washington, on March 31, 1971,<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> by three partners who met while they were students at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_San_Francisco" title="University of San Francisco">University of San Francisco</a>:<sup id="cite_ref-TimeOutSF_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TimeOutSF-22">[22]</a></sup> English teacher <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Baldwin" title="Jerry Baldwin">Jerry Baldwin</a>, history teacher <a href="/wiki/Zev_Siegl" title="Zev Siegl">Zev Siegl</a>, and writer <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Bowker" title="Gordon Bowker">Gordon Bowker</a> were inspired to sell high-quality coffee beans and equipment by coffee roasting entrepreneur <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Peet" title="Alfred Peet">Alfred Peet</a> after he taught them his style of roasting beans.<sup id="cite_ref-Pren2523_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pren2523-23">[23]</a></sup> Bowker recalls that Terry Heckler, with whom Bowker owned an advertising agency, thought words beginning with "st" were powerful. The founders brainstormed a list of words beginning with "st," and eventually landed on "Starbo," a mining town in the <a href="/wiki/Cascade_Range" title="Cascade Range">Cascade Range</a>. From there, the group remembered "Starbuck," the name of the <a href="/wiki/Chief_mate" title="Chief mate">chief mate</a> in the book <i><a href="/wiki/Moby-Dick" title="Moby-Dick">Moby-Dick</a>.</i><sup id="cite_ref-:4_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-24">[24]</a></sup> Bowker said, "<i>Moby-Dick</i> didn't have anything to do with Starbucks directly; it was only coincidental that the sound seemed to make sense."<sup id="cite_ref-:4_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-24">[24]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p><p>The first Starbucks store was located in Seattle at 2000 Western Avenue from 1971–1976. This cafe was later moved to 1912 Pike Place.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> During this time, the company only sold roasted whole coffee beans and did not yet brew coffee to sell.<sup id="cite_ref-usa1992_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usa1992-27">[27]</a></sup> During their first year of operation, they purchased green coffee beans from <a href="/wiki/Peet%27s_Coffee_%26_Tea" class="mw-redirect" title="Peet's Coffee &amp; Tea">Peet's</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> then began buying directly from growers.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Sale_and_expansion">Sale and expansion</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chinatown_Starbucks_(48126613907).jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Chinatown_Starbucks_%2848126613907%29.jpg/170px-Chinatown_Starbucks_%2848126613907%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2942" data-file-height="3923"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 170px;height: 227px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Chinatown_Starbucks_%2848126613907%29.jpg/170px-Chinatown_Starbucks_%2848126613907%29.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="170" data-height="227" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chinatown_Starbucks_(48126613907).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Chinese-style Starbucks in <a href="/wiki/Chinatown,_Manhattan" title="Chinatown, Manhattan">Chinatown, Manhattan</a>, New York</div></div></div>
<p>In 1984, the original owners of Starbucks, led by <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Baldwin" title="Jerry Baldwin">Jerry Baldwin</a>, purchased Peet's.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> During the 1980s, total sales of coffee in the US were falling, but sales of <a href="/wiki/Specialty_coffee" title="Specialty coffee">specialty coffee</a> increased, forming 10% of the market in 1989, compared with 3% in 1983.<sup id="cite_ref-wsj1989_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj1989-30">[30]</a></sup> By 1986, the company operated six stores in Seattle<sup id="cite_ref-wsj1989_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj1989-30">[30]</a></sup> and had only just begun to sell <a href="/wiki/Espresso" title="Espresso">espresso</a> coffee.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p><p>In 1987, the original owners sold the Starbucks chain to former manager<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Howard_Schultz" title="Howard Schultz">Howard Schultz</a>, who rebranded his Il Giornale coffee outlets as Starbucks and quickly began to expand. In the same year, Starbucks opened its first locations outside Seattle at <a href="/wiki/Waterfront_Station_(Vancouver)" class="mw-redirect" title="Waterfront Station (Vancouver)">Waterfront Station</a> in <a href="/wiki/Vancouver" title="Vancouver">Vancouver</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia" title="British Columbia">British Columbia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a>, Illinois.<sup id="cite_ref-tele40_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tele40-33">[33]</a></sup> By 1989, 46 stores existed across the Northwest and <a href="/wiki/Midwest" class="mw-redirect" title="Midwest">Midwest</a>, and annually Starbucks was roasting over 2,000,000 pounds (907,185 kg) of coffee.<sup id="cite_ref-wsj1989_30-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj1989-30">[30]</a></sup></p><p>At the time of its <a href="/wiki/Initial_public_offering" title="Initial public offering">initial public offering</a> (IPO) on the stock market in June 1992, Starbucks had 140 outlets, with revenue of <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>73.5 million, up from US$1.3 million in 1987. The company's market value was US$271 million by this time. The 12% portion of the company that was sold raised around US$25 million for the company, which facilitated a doubling of the number of stores over the next two years.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> By September 1992, Starbucks's share price had risen by 70% to over 100 times the <a href="/wiki/Earnings_per_share" title="Earnings per share">earnings per share</a> of the previous year.<sup id="cite_ref-usa1992_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usa1992-27">[27]</a></sup></p><p>In July 2013, over 10% of in-store purchases were made on customer's mobile devices using the <span id="Starbucks_app">Starbucks app</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> The company once again utilized the mobile platform when it launched the "Tweet-a-Coffee" promotion in October 2013. On this occasion, the promotion also involved <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> and customers were able to purchase a US$5 gift card for a friend by entering both "@tweetacoffee" and the friend's handle in a <a href="/wiki/Tweet_(Twitter)#Tweets" class="mw-redirect" title="Tweet (Twitter)">tweet</a>. Research firm Keyhole monitored the progress of the campaign and a December 6, 2013, media article reported that the firm had found that 27,000 people had participated and US$180,000 of purchases were made to date.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> As of 2018, Starbucks is ranked 132nd on the <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a> list of the largest United States corporations by revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p><p>In July 2019, Starbucks reported "fiscal third-quarter net income of $1.37 billion, or $1.12 per share, up from $852.5 million, or 61 cents per share, a year earlier." The company's market value of $110.2 billion increased by 41% in the mid 2019. The earnings per share in quarter three were recorded 78 cents, much more than the forecast of 72 cents.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>

</td>
<td>2,818
</td>
<td>14,313
</td>
<td>54.17
</td>
<td>254,000
</td></tr><tr><td>2017
</td>
<td>22,387
</td>
<td>2,885
</td>
<td>14,366
</td>
<td>55.75
</td>
<td>277,000
</td></tr></tbody></table><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Expansion_to_new_markets_and_products">Expansion to new markets and products</span></h3>
<p>The first Starbucks location outside North America opened in <a href="/wiki/Tokyo,_Japan" class="mw-redirect" title="Tokyo, Japan">Tokyo, Japan</a>, in 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> On December 4, 1997, the Philippines became the third market to open outside North America with its first branch in the country located at 6750 Ayala Building in <a href="/wiki/Makati" title="Makati">Makati City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> Starbucks entered the U.K. market in 1998 with the $83 million<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> USD acquisition of the then 56-outlet, UK-based Seattle Coffee Company, re-branding all the stores as Starbucks.
</p><p>In 1999, Starbucks experimented with eateries in the San Francisco Bay area through a restaurant chain called Circadia. After people learned that these restaurants were owned by Starbucks, Starbucks converted the restaurants to Starbucks cafes.<sup id="cite_ref-circadia_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-circadia-45">[45]</a></sup></p><p>Australia's first Starbucks store opened in July 2000 in <a href="/wiki/Sydney" title="Sydney">Sydney</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> After a massive downturn in 2008, the remaining Australian Starbucks stores were purchased in 2014, with the company planning a more restrained expansion.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p><p>In September 2002, Starbucks opened its first store in Latin America, at <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">Mexico City</a>. Currently, there are over 500 locations in <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a> and there are plans for the opening of up to 850 by 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p><p>In October 2002, Starbucks established a coffee trading company in <a href="/wiki/Lausanne" title="Lausanne">Lausanne</a>, Switzerland to handle purchases of <a href="/wiki/Green_coffee" class="mw-redirect" title="Green coffee">green coffee</a>. All other coffee-related business continued to be managed from Seattle.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p><p>In April 2003, Starbucks completed the purchase of <a href="/wiki/Seattle%27s_Best_Coffee" title="Seattle's Best Coffee">Seattle's Best Coffee</a> and <a href="/wiki/Torrefazione_Italia" title="Torrefazione Italia">Torrefazione Italia</a> from <a href="/wiki/AFC_Enterprises" class="mw-redirect" title="AFC Enterprises">AFC Enterprises</a> for $72m. The deal only gained 150 stores for Starbucks, but according to the <i><a href="/wiki/Seattle_Post-Intelligencer" title="Seattle Post-Intelligencer">Seattle Post-Intelligencer</a>,</i> the wholesale business was more significant.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> In September 2006, rival <a href="/wiki/Diedrich_Coffee" title="Diedrich Coffee">Diedrich Coffee</a> announced that it would sell most of its company-owned retail stores to Starbucks. This sale included the company-owned locations of the Oregon-based <a href="/wiki/Diedrich_Coffee" title="Diedrich Coffee">Coffee People</a> chain. Starbucks converted the Diedrich Coffee and Coffee People locations to Starbucks, although the <a href="/wiki/Portland_International_Airport" title="Portland International Airport">Portland International Airport</a> Coffee People locations were excluded from the sale.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p><p>In August 2003, Starbucks opened its first store in South America in <a href="/wiki/Lima" title="Lima">Lima</a>, Peru.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p><p>In 2007, the company opened its first store in Russia, ten years after first registering a trademark there.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-54">[54]</a></sup></p><p>In 2008, they purchased the manufacturer of the <a href="/wiki/Clover_Equipment_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Clover Equipment Company">Clover Brewing System</a>. They began testing the "fresh-pressed" coffee system at several Starbucks locations in Seattle, California, New York, and Boston.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Starbucks_stores_graph.png" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Starbucks_stores_graph.png/220px-Starbucks_stores_graph.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="668" data-file-height="437"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 144px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Starbucks_stores_graph.png/220px-Starbucks_stores_graph.png" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="144" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Starbucks_stores_graph.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Graph showing the growth in the number of Starbucks stores between 1971 and 2011<sup id="cite_ref-tele40_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tele40-33">[33]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>In early 2008, Starbucks started a community website, My Starbucks Idea, designed to collect suggestions and feedback from customers. Other users comment and vote on suggestions. Journalist Jack Schofield noted that "My Starbucks seems to be all sweetness and light at the moment, which I don't think is possible without quite a lot of censorship."<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></p><p>In May 2008, a <a href="/wiki/Loyalty_program" title="Loyalty program">loyalty program</a> was introduced for registered users of the Starbucks Card (previously simply a gift card) offering perks such as free <a href="/wiki/Wi-Fi" title="Wi-Fi">Wi-Fi</a> Internet access, no charge for soy milk and flavored syrups, and free refills on brewed drip coffee, iced coffee, or tea.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> In 2009, Starbucks began beta testing its mobile app for the Starbucks card, a stored value system in which consumers access pre-paid funds to purchase products at Starbucks.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> Starbucks released its complete mobile platform on January 11, 2011.
</p><p>On November 14, 2012, Starbucks announced the purchase of <a href="/wiki/Teavana" title="Teavana">Teavana</a> for US$620 million in cash<sup id="cite_ref-baertlein2012_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-baertlein2012-59">[59]</a></sup> and the deal was formally closed on December 31, 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-Melissa_Allison_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Melissa_Allison-60">[60]</a></sup></p><p>On February 1, 2013, Starbucks opened its first store in <a href="/wiki/Ho_Chi_Minh_City" title="Ho Chi Minh City">Ho Chi Minh City</a>, Vietnam,<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> and this was followed by an announcement in late August 2013 that the retailer will be opening its inaugural store in <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>. The Colombian announcement was delivered at a press conference in Bogota, where the company's CEO explained, "Starbucks has always admired and respected Colombia's distinguished coffee tradition."<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p><p>In May 2014, the Starbucks operations in South Korea launched a mobile ordering system named Siren Order, which is accessible through a local version of Starbucks smartphone application.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> Starbucks in the U.S. later launched a similar system named Mobile Order &amp; Pay, starting with Portland, Oregon in December 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> The service have since expanded nationwide, and in late March 2018, the company opened the system (previously available to Starbucks Rewards members only) to all customers.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p><p>In August 2014, Starbucks opened their first store in <a href="/wiki/Williamsburg,_Brooklyn" title="Williamsburg, Brooklyn">Williamsburg</a>, Brooklyn. This location will be one of 30 Starbucks stores that will serve beer and wine.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p><p>In September 2014, it was revealed that Starbucks would acquire the remaining 60.5 percent stake in Starbuck Coffee Japan that it does not already own, at a price of $913.5 million.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p><p>In August 2015, Starbucks announced that it will enter Cambodia, its 16th market in the China/Asia Pacific region. The first location will open in the capital city of Phnom Penh by the end of 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></p><p>In February 2016, Starbucks announced that it will enter Italy, its 24th market in Europe. The first location will open in Milan by 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> In August, <a href="/wiki/Startup_company" title="Startup company">startup company</a> FluxPort introduced <a href="/wiki/Qi_(standard)" title="Qi (standard)">Qi</a> <a href="/wiki/Inductive_charging" title="Inductive charging">inductive charging</a> pads at select locations in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p><p>In September 2016, Starbucks announced a debut of its first-ever original content series called "Upstanders" which aims to inspire Americans with stories of compassion, citizenship, and civility. The series features podcasts, written word, and video, and will be distributed via the Starbucks mobile app, online, and through the company's in-store digital network.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p><p>On July 27, 2017, Starbucks acquired the remaining 50% stake in their Chinese venture from long-term joint venture partners Uni-President Enterprises Corporation (UPEC) and President Chain Store Corporation (PCSC).<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p><p>On March 21, 2018, Starbucks announced that it is considering the use of <a href="/wiki/Blockchain" title="Blockchain">blockchain</a> technology with an idea to connect coffee drinkers with coffee farmers who eventually can take advantage of new financial opportunities. The <a href="/wiki/Pilot_program" class="mw-redirect" title="Pilot program">pilot program</a> is going to start with farmers in <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica" title="Costa Rica">Costa Rica</a>, Colombia and Rwanda in order to develop a new way to track the bean to cup journey.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p><p>On June 19, 2018, Starbucks announced the closing of 150 locations in 2019, this is three times the number the corporation typically closes in a single year. The closings will happen in <a href="/wiki/Urban_areas" class="mw-redirect" title="Urban areas">urban areas</a> that already have dense clusters of stores.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p><p>In 2018, Starbucks expanded its partnership with <a href="/wiki/Uber_Eats" title="Uber Eats">Uber Eats</a> to bring its beverages to U.S. customers' doorsteps, as it had already done for some time in China.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p><p>In November 2019, Starbucks opened its biggest store ever on <a href="/wiki/Michigan_Avenue_(Chicago)" title="Michigan Avenue (Chicago)">Michigan Avenue</a>, Chicago. The store is open seven days a week and has 200 employees.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p><p>On 20 March 2020, due to the <a href="/wiki/2019-20_coronavirus_pandemic" class="mw-redirect" title="2019-20 coronavirus pandemic">2019-20 coronavirus pandemic</a> outbreak, Starbucks decided to close all the cafe-only stores in the United States for two weeks. During that time, only drive-thru- and delivery-only will function. According to the company representatives, all workers will be paid for the next 30 days whether they go to work or stay home.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(2)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_governance">Corporate governance</span></h2><section class="mf-section-2 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-2">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Howard-Schultz-Starbucks_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Howard-Schultz-Starbucks_%28cropped%29.jpg/170px-Howard-Schultz-Starbucks_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="239" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="847" data-file-height="1191"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 170px;height: 239px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Howard-Schultz-Starbucks_%28cropped%29.jpg/170px-Howard-Schultz-Starbucks_%28cropped%29.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="170" data-height="239" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Howard-Schultz-Starbucks_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Howard_Schultz" title="Howard Schultz">Howard Schultz</a>, Chairman Emeritus of Starbucks</div></div></div>
<p>In 2006, Starbucks's chairman at the time, <a href="/wiki/Howard_Schultz" title="Howard Schultz">Howard Schultz</a>, talked about making sure growth does not dilute the <a href="/wiki/Company_culture" class="mw-redirect" title="Company culture">company's culture</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></p><p>Howard Schultz served as the company's CEO until 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-lerman2015b_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lerman2015b-85">[85]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Orin_C._Smith" title="Orin C. Smith">Orin C. Smith</a> was President and CEO of Starbucks from 2001 to 2005.
</p><p>In January 2008, Schultz resumed his roles as President and CEO after an eight-year hiatus, replacing <a href="/wiki/Jim_Donald_(CEO)" class="mw-redirect" title="Jim Donald (CEO)">Jim Donald</a>, who took the posts in 2005 but was asked to step down after sales slowed in 2007. Schultz aims to restore what he calls the "distinctive Starbucks experience" in the face of rapid expansion. Analysts believe that Schultz must determine how to contend with higher materials prices and enhanced competition from lower-priced fast-food chains, including <a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s" title="McDonald's">McDonald's</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dunkin%27_Donuts" title="Dunkin' Donuts">Dunkin' Donuts</a>. Starbucks announced it would discontinue the warm breakfast sandwich products they originally intended to launch nationwide in 2008 and refocus on coffee, but they reformulated the sandwiches to deal with complaints and kept the product line.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p><p>As of January 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Starbucks&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the <a href="/wiki/Chief_operating_officer" title="Chief operating officer">chief operating officer</a> of Starbucks was Troy Alstead, though at that time he announced he was taking an extended leave of absence of undetermined length.<sup id="cite_ref-lerman2015b_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lerman2015b-85">[85]</a></sup> Subsequently, <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Johnson_(executive)" title="Kevin Johnson (executive)">Kevin Johnson</a> was appointed to succeed Alstead as president and COO.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p><p>In October 2015, Starbucks hired its first Chief Technology Officer, Gerri Martin-Flickinger, to lead its technology team.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> In April 2017, Schultz became executive chairman of Starbucks with Johnson becoming President and CEO.
</p><p>Starbucks maintains control of production processes by communicating with farmers to secure beans, roasting its own beans, and managing distribution to all retail locations. Additionally, Starbucks's Coffee and Farmer Equity Practices require suppliers to inform Starbucks what portion of wholesale prices paid reaches farmers.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Stanley,_A._2002_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stanley,_A._2002-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(3)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Products">Products</span></h2><section class="mf-section-3 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-3">
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Starbucksdesk.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Starbucksdesk.jpg/220px-Starbucksdesk.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Starbucksdesk.jpg/220px-Starbucksdesk.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="165" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Starbucksdesk.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A typical sales area, this one in <a href="/wiki/Peterborough" title="Peterborough">Peterborough</a>, UK, showing a display of food and the beverage preparation area</div></div></div>
<p>In 1994, Starbucks bought <a href="/wiki/The_Coffee_Connection" class="mw-redirect" title="The Coffee Connection">The Coffee Connection</a>, gaining the rights to use, make, market, and sell the "<a href="/wiki/Frappuccino" title="Frappuccino">Frappuccino</a>" beverage.<sup id="cite_ref-BosMag_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BosMag-91">[91]</a></sup> The beverage was introduced under the Starbucks name in 1995 and as of 2012, Starbucks had annual Frappuccinos sales of over $2 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-BosMag_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BosMag-91">[91]</a></sup></p><p>The company began a "skinny" line of drinks in 2008, offering <a href="/wiki/Low_calorie" class="mw-redirect" title="Low calorie">lower-calorie</a> and sugar-free versions of the company's offered drinks that use <a href="/wiki/Skim_milk" class="mw-redirect" title="Skim milk">skim milk</a>, and can be sweetened by a choice of natural sweeteners (such as <a href="/wiki/Raw_sugar" class="mw-redirect" title="Raw sugar">raw sugar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Agave_syrup" title="Agave syrup">agave syrup</a>, or honey), <a href="/wiki/Sugar_substitute" title="Sugar substitute">artificial sweeteners</a> (such as <a href="/wiki/Sweet%27N_Low" class="mw-redirect" title="Sweet'N Low">Sweet'N Low</a>, <a href="/wiki/Splenda" title="Splenda">Splenda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Equal_(sweetener)" title="Equal (sweetener)">Equal</a>), or one of the company's <a href="/wiki/Sugar-free" class="mw-redirect" title="Sugar-free">sugar-free</a> syrup flavors.<sup id="cite_ref-Low-Cal_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Low-Cal-92">[92]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Skinny_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skinny-93">[93]</a></sup> Starbucks stopped using milk originating from <a href="/wiki/RBGH" class="mw-redirect" title="RBGH">rBGH</a>-treated cows in 2007.
</p><p>In June 2009, the company announced that it would be overhauling its menu and selling salads and baked goods without <a href="/wiki/High_fructose_corn_syrup" class="mw-redirect" title="High fructose corn syrup">high fructose corn syrup</a> or artificial ingredients.<sup id="cite_ref-stars_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stars-94">[94]</a></sup> This move was expected to attract health- and cost-conscious consumers and will not affect prices.<sup id="cite_ref-stars_94-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stars-94">[94]</a></sup></p><p>Starbucks introduced a new line of instant coffee packets, called VIA "Ready Brew," in March 2009. It was first unveiled in New York City with subsequent testing of the product also in <a href="/wiki/Seattle" title="Seattle">Seattle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a>, and <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>. The first two VIA flavors include Italian Roast and Colombia, which were then rolled out in October 2009, across the U.S. and Canada with Starbucks stores promoting the product with a <a href="/wiki/Blind_study" class="mw-redirect" title="Blind study">blind</a> "taste challenge" of the instant versus fresh roast, in which many people could not tell the difference between the instant and freshly brewed coffee. Analysts<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (May 2013)">who?</span></a></i>]</sup> speculated that by introducing instant coffee, Starbucks would devalue its own brand.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup></p><p>Starbucks began selling beer and wine at some US stores in 2010. As of April 2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Starbucks&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, it is available at seven locations and others have applied for licenses.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></p><p>In 2011, Starbucks introduced its largest cup size, the Trenta, which can hold 31 US fluid ounces (920 ml).<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> In September 2012, Starbucks announced the Verismo, a consumer-grade single-serve coffee machine that uses sealed plastic cups of coffee grounds, and a "milk pod" for lattes.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></p><p>On November 10, 2011, Starbucks Corporation announced that it had bought juice company <a href="/wiki/Evolution_Fresh" title="Evolution Fresh">Evolution Fresh</a> for $30 million in cash and planned to start a chain of juice bars starting in around the middle of 2012, venturing into territory staked out by <a href="/wiki/Jamba_Juice" title="Jamba Juice">Jamba Inc</a>. Its first store released in San Bernardino, California and plans for a store in San Francisco were to be launched in early 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></p><p>In 2012, Starbucks began selling a line of iced Starbucks Refresher beverages that contain an extract from <a href="/wiki/Green_coffee" class="mw-redirect" title="Green coffee">green arabica coffee beans</a>. The beverages are fruit flavored and contain <a href="/wiki/Caffeine" title="Caffeine">caffeine</a> but advertised as having no coffee flavor. Starbucks's green coffee extraction process involves soaking the beans in water.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></p><p>On June 25, 2013, Starbucks began to post calorie counts on menus for drinks and pastries in all of their U.S. stores.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup></p><p>In 2014, Starbucks began producing their own line of sodas, dubbed "Fizzio."<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></p><p>In 2015, Starbucks began serving <a href="/wiki/Coconut_milk" title="Coconut milk">coconut milk</a> as an alternative to dairy and soy.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></p><p>In March 2017, Starbucks announced the launch of two new limited-edition specialty drinks made from beans aged in whiskey barrels at its Seattle roastery.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> Starbucks's barrel-aged coffee will be sold with a small batch of unroasted <a href="/wiki/Starbucks_Reserve" title="Starbucks Reserve">Starbucks Reserve</a> Sulawesi beans, which are then hand-scooped into whiskey barrels from <a href="/wiki/Washington_D.C." class="mw-redirect" title="Washington D.C.">Washington D.C.</a><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<table class="wikitable"><tbody><tr><th>Name
</th>
<th>Measurement
</th>
<th>Notes
</th></tr><tr><td>Demi
</td>
<td>3 US fl oz (89 ml)
</td>
<td>Smallest size. Espresso shots.
</td></tr><tr><td>Short
</td>
<td>8 US fl oz (240 ml)
</td>
<td>Smaller of the two original sizes

</td></tr></tbody></table><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Tea">Tea</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Starbucks_Truck_NJ_Turnpike.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Starbucks_Truck_NJ_Turnpike.jpg/220px-Starbucks_Truck_NJ_Turnpike.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="4160" data-file-height="3120"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Starbucks_Truck_NJ_Turnpike.jpg/220px-Starbucks_Truck_NJ_Turnpike.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="165" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Starbucks_Truck_NJ_Turnpike.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Starbucks <a href="/wiki/Food_truck" title="Food truck">food truck</a> in a rest area on the <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Turnpike" title="New Jersey Turnpike">New Jersey Turnpike</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Starbucks entered the tea business in 1999 when it acquired the <a href="/wiki/Tazo" title="Tazo">Tazo</a> brand for <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>8,100,000.<sup id="cite_ref-psbj2012_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-psbj2012-107">[107]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-jargon2012_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jargon2012-108">[108]</a></sup> In late 2012, Starbucks paid US$620 million to buy <a href="/wiki/Teavana" title="Teavana">Teavana</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Melissa_Allison_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Melissa_Allison-60">[60]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> As of November 2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Starbucks&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there is no intention of marketing Starbucks's products in Teavana stores, though the acquisition will allow the expansion of Teavana beyond its current main footprint in <a href="/wiki/Shopping_mall" title="Shopping mall">shopping malls</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-jargon2012_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jargon2012-108">[108]</a></sup> In January 2015, Starbucks began to roll out Teavana teas into Starbucks stores, both in to-go beverage and retail formats.<sup id="cite_ref-sbux2015_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sbux2015-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Coffee_quality">Coffee quality</span></h3>
<p>Kevin Knox, who was in charge of doughnuts <a href="/wiki/Food_quality" title="Food quality">quality</a> at Starbucks from 1987 to 1993, recalled on his blog in 2010 how <a href="/wiki/George_Howell_(entrepreneur)" title="George Howell (entrepreneur)">George Howell</a>, coffee veteran and founder of the <a href="/wiki/Cup_of_Excellence" title="Cup of Excellence">Cup of Excellence</a>, had been appalled at the <a href="/wiki/Coffee_roasting#Roast_flavors" title="Coffee roasting">dark roasted</a> beans that Starbucks was selling in 1990.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-55">[55]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> Talking to the <i>New York Times</i> in 2008, Howell stated his opinion that the dark roast used by Starbucks does not deepen the flavor of coffee, but instead can destroy purported nuances of flavor.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_55-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-55">[55]</a></sup> The March 2007 issue of <i><a href="/wiki/Consumer_Reports" title="Consumer Reports">Consumer Reports</a></i> compared American fast-food chain coffees and ranked Starbucks behind <a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s" title="McDonald's">McDonald's</a> Premium Roast. The magazine called Starbucks coffee "strong, but burnt and bitter enough to make your eyes water instead of open."<sup id="cite_ref-msnbc_16951509_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-msnbc_16951509-112">[112]</a></sup> As reported by <i>TIME</i> in 2010, third wave coffee proponents generally criticize Starbucks for over-roasting beans.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Starbucks_Verismo">Starbucks Verismo</span></h3>
<p>In 2012, Starbucks introduced Starbucks Verismo, a line of coffee makers that brew espresso and regular chocolate from coffee capsules, a type of pre-apportioned <a href="/wiki/Disposable_product" title="Disposable product">single-use</a> container of ground coffee and flavorings utilizing the K-Fee pod system.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> In a brief review of the 580 model, <a href="/wiki/Consumer_Reports" title="Consumer Reports">Consumer Reports</a> described the results of a comparative test of the Verismo 580 against two competitive brands: "Because you have to conduct a rinse cycle between each cup, the Verismo wasn't among the most convenient of single-serve machines in our coffeemaker tests. Other machines we've tested have more flexibility in adjusting brew-strength—the Verismo has buttons for coffee, espresso, and latte with no strength variation for any type. And since Starbucks has limited its coffee selection to its own brand, there are only eight varieties so far plus a milk pod for the latte."<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_products">Other products</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lody_marki_Starbucks.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Lody_marki_Starbucks.jpg/220px-Lody_marki_Starbucks.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1440"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 124px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Lody_marki_Starbucks.jpg/220px-Lody_marki_Starbucks.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="124" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lody_marki_Starbucks.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ice creams of Starbucks</div></div></div>
<p>In July 2019, Starbucks announced that it would no longer be selling newspapers in its cafes. It was also announced that kiosks for grab-and-go snacks and bags of whole-bean coffee would be removed from stores beginning in September 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(4)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Locations">Locations</span></h2><section class="mf-section-4 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-4">
<p>The company's headquarters is located in <a href="/wiki/Seattle" title="Seattle">Seattle</a>, Washington, United States, where 3,501 people worked as of January 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-lerman2015_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lerman2015-117">[117]</a></sup> The main building in the Starbucks complex was previously a Sears distribution center.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Current">Current</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:604px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Starbucks_(Updated_as_of_2019).png" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Starbucks_%28Updated_as_of_2019%29.png/602px-Starbucks_%28Updated_as_of_2019%29.png" decoding="async" width="602" height="256" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="6000" data-file-height="2552"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 602px;height: 256px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Starbucks_%28Updated_as_of_2019%29.png/602px-Starbucks_%28Updated_as_of_2019%29.png" data-alt="" data-width="602" data-height="256" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Starbucks_(Updated_as_of_2019).png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>International Presence of Starbucks Coffee (June 2019).</div></div></div>
<p>As of November 2019, Starbucks is present on 6 continents and in 78 countries and territories, with around 31,256 Locations:<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></p>

<li><a href="/wiki/Uruguay" title="Uruguay">Uruguay</a>: 1</li></ul></td></tr></tbody></table><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Expansion">Expansion</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Starbucks_Cafe_in_Warsaw,_Poland.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Starbucks_Cafe_in_Warsaw%2C_Poland.jpg/220px-Starbucks_Cafe_in_Warsaw%2C_Poland.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Starbucks_Cafe_in_Warsaw%2C_Poland.jpg/220px-Starbucks_Cafe_in_Warsaw%2C_Poland.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="165" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Starbucks_Cafe_in_Warsaw,_Poland.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Starbucks Cafe in <a href="/wiki/Warsaw" title="Warsaw">Warsaw</a>, Poland</div></div></div>
<p>In 2008, Starbucks continued its expansion, settling in Argentina, Belgium, Brazil, Bulgaria, the Czech Republic, and Portugal.<sup id="cite_ref-tele40_33-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tele40-33">[33]</a></sup></p><p>European and Scandinavian expansion continued in 2009 with Poland (April),<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> Utrecht, Netherlands (August), and Sweden at <a href="/wiki/Arlanda_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Arlanda Airport">Arlanda Airport</a> outside <a href="/wiki/Stockholm" title="Stockholm">Stockholm</a> (October).<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></p><p>In 2010, growth in new markets continued. In May 2010, Southern Sun Hotels South Africa announced that they had signed an agreement with Starbucks to brew Starbucks coffees in select Southern Sun and Tsonga Sun hotels in South Africa. The agreement was partially reached so Starbucks coffees could be served in the country in time for the 2010 FIFA World Cup hosted by South Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> In June 2010, Starbucks opened its first store in <a href="/wiki/Budapest" title="Budapest">Budapest</a>, Hungary and in November, the company opened the first Central American store in El Salvador's capital, <a href="/wiki/San_Salvador" title="San Salvador">San Salvador</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup></p><p>In December 2010, Starbucks debuted their first-ever Starbucks at sea, wherewith a partnership with <a href="/wiki/Royal_Caribbean_International" title="Royal Caribbean International">Royal Caribbean International</a>; Starbucks opened a shop aboard their <a href="/wiki/Allure_of_the_Seas" title="Allure of the Seas">Allure of the Seas</a> Royal Caribbean's second-largest ship, and also the second-largest ship in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup></p><p>Starbucks is planning to open<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (July 2012)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> its fourth African location, after South Africa, Egypt, and Morocco, in Algeria. A partnership with Algerian food company <a href="/wiki/Cevital" title="Cevital">Cevital</a> will see Starbucks open its first Algerian store in <a href="/wiki/Algiers" title="Algiers">Algiers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup></p><p>In January 2011, Starbucks and <a href="/wiki/Tata_Coffee" title="Tata Coffee">Tata Coffee</a>, Asia's largest coffee plantation company, announced plans for a strategic alliance to bring Starbucks to <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> and also to source and roast coffee beans at Tata Coffee's <a href="/wiki/Kodagu" class="mw-redirect" title="Kodagu">Kodagu</a> facility.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> Despite a false start in 2007,<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> in January 2012, Starbucks announced a 50:50 joint venture with <a href="/wiki/Tata_Global_Beverages" class="mw-redirect" title="Tata Global Beverages">Tata Global Beverages</a> called <a href="/wiki/Tata_Starbucks" title="Tata Starbucks">Tata Starbucks</a>. Tata Starbucks will own and operate Starbucks outlets in India as <i>Starbucks Coffee "A Tata Alliance."</i><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> Starbucks opened its first store in India in <a href="/wiki/Mumbai" title="Mumbai">Mumbai</a> on October 19, 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Starbucks_at_the_Forbidden_City.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Starbucks_at_the_Forbidden_City.jpg/220px-Starbucks_at_the_Forbidden_City.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2288" data-file-height="1520"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 146px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Starbucks_at_the_Forbidden_City.jpg/220px-Starbucks_at_the_Forbidden_City.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="146" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Starbucks_at_the_Forbidden_City.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Starbucks at the <a href="/wiki/Forbidden_City" title="Forbidden City">Forbidden City</a>, Beijing, China</div></div></div>
<p>In February 2011, Starbucks started selling its coffee in Norway by supplying Norwegian food shops with their roasts. The first Starbucks-branded Norwegian shop opened on February 8, 2012, at <a href="/wiki/Oslo_Airport,_Gardermoen" title="Oslo Airport, Gardermoen">Oslo Airport, Gardermoen</a>. In October 2011, Starbucks opened another location in Beijing, China, at the <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Capital_International_Airport" title="Beijing Capital International Airport">Beijing Capital International Airport</a>'s Terminal 3, international departures hall; making the company's 500th store in China. The store is the 7th location at the airport. The company planned to expand to 1,500 stores in China by 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> In May 2012, Starbucks opened its first coffeehouse in <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a>, with the location being <a href="/wiki/Helsinki-Vantaa_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Helsinki-Vantaa Airport">Helsinki-Vantaa Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Vantaa" title="Vantaa">Vantaa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> In June 2012, Starbucks opened a store in <a href="/wiki/San_Jose,_Costa_Rica" class="mw-redirect" title="San Jose, Costa Rica">San Jose,</a> Costa Rica.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup></p><p>In October 2012, Starbucks announced plans to open 1,000 stores in the United States in the next five years.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> The same month, the largest Starbucks in the US opened at the University of Alabama's Ferguson Center.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup></p><p>In 2013, Starbucks met with <a href="/wiki/Dansk_Supermarked" class="mw-redirect" title="Dansk Supermarked">Dansk Supermarked</a>, which is the biggest retail company in Denmark. The first Starbucks inside Dansk Supermarked opened in August 2013 in the department stores Salling in <a href="/wiki/Aalborg" title="Aalborg">Aalborg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aarhus" title="Aarhus">Aarhus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup></p><p>Starbucks has announced its first café in Bolivia would open in 2014 in <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_de_la_Sierra" title="Santa Cruz de la Sierra">Santa Cruz de la Sierra</a> and the first in Panama in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup></p><p>On June 19, 2015, a Starbucks opened at <a href="/wiki/Disney%27s_Animal_Kingdom" title="Disney's Animal Kingdom">Disney's Animal Kingdom</a> on <a href="/wiki/Discovery_Island_(Disney%27s_Animal_Kingdom)" class="mw-redirect" title="Discovery Island (Disney's Animal Kingdom)">Discovery Island</a>. Since the park does not allow plastic straws due to the animals, this location features special green eco-friendly straws with their cold drinks.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> This was the sixth Starbucks to open in <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_World" title="Walt Disney World">Walt Disney World</a>, following locations in the <a href="/wiki/Magic_Kingdom" title="Magic Kingdom">Magic Kingdom</a> (<a href="/wiki/Main_Street,_U.S.A.#Magic_Kingdom" title="Main Street, U.S.A.">Main Street, U.S.A.</a>), <a href="/wiki/Epcot" title="Epcot">Epcot</a> (<a href="/wiki/Epcot#Future_World" title="Epcot">Future World</a>), <a href="/wiki/Disney%27s_Hollywood_Studios" title="Disney's Hollywood Studios">Disney's Hollywood Studios</a> (<a href="/wiki/Disney%27s_Hollywood_Studios#Hollywood_Boulevard" title="Disney's Hollywood Studios">Hollywood Boulevard</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-Disney's_Hollywood_Studios_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Disney's_Hollywood_Studios-141">[141]</a></sup> and two in <a href="/wiki/Disney_Springs" title="Disney Springs">Disney Springs</a> (<a href="/wiki/Disney_Springs#Marketplace" title="Disney Springs">Marketplace</a> and <a href="/wiki/Characters_in_Flight" class="mw-redirect" title="Characters in Flight">West Side</a>). In addition to these six, there are locations in <a href="/wiki/Disneyland" title="Disneyland">Disneyland</a> (<a href="/wiki/Main_Street,_U.S.A.#Disneyland_Park" title="Main Street, U.S.A.">Main Street, U.S.A.</a>), <a href="/wiki/Disney_California_Adventure" title="Disney California Adventure">Disney California Adventure</a> (<a href="/wiki/Buena_Vista_Street" title="Buena Vista Street">Buena Vista Street</a>), Anaheim's <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Disney_(Disneyland_Resort)" class="mw-redirect" title="Downtown Disney (Disneyland Resort)">Downtown Disney</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Disney_Village" title="Disney Village">Disney Village</a> at <a href="/wiki/Disneyland_Paris" title="Disneyland Paris">Disneyland Paris</a>. The Downtown Disney and Disney Springs locations are Starbucks-operated, while the locations inside of the theme parks are Disney-operated.<sup id="cite_ref-Disney_Starbucks_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Disney_Starbucks-142">[142]</a></sup></p><p>Bill Sleeth, Starbucks's vice president of global design, has overseen efforts to make a neighborhood feel for new stores, saying "What you don't want is a customer walking into a store in downtown Seattle, walking into a store in the suburbs of Seattle and then going into a store in San Jose, and seeing the same store." Sleeth said "The customers were saying, 'Everywhere I go, there you are,' and not in a good way. We were pretty ubiquitous." As part of a change in compact direction, Starbucks management wanted to transition from the singular brand worldwide to focusing on locally relevant design for each store.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup></p><p>Starbucks's first Channel Island store was opened in early 2015, in the primary business area of <a href="/wiki/St_Peter_Port" class="mw-redirect" title="St Peter Port">St Peter Port</a> in <a href="/wiki/Guernsey" title="Guernsey">Guernsey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup></p><p>In 2014 Starbucks was scheduled to open a store in <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a>, in the Port Baku Mall.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup></p><p>In August 2013, Starbucks's CEO, <a href="/wiki/Howard_Schultz" title="Howard Schultz">Howard Schultz</a>, personally announced the opening of Starbucks stores in <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>. The first café was set to open in 2014 in <a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1" title="Bogotá">Bogotá</a> and add 50 more stores throughout Colombia's main cities in a 5-year limit. Schultz also stated that Starbucks will work with both the Colombian Government and <a href="/wiki/USAID" class="mw-redirect" title="USAID">USAID</a> to continue "empowering local coffee growers and sharing the value, heritage and tradition of its coffee with the world." Starbucks noted that the aggressive expansion into Colombia was a joint venture with Starbucks's Latin partners, <a href="/wiki/Alsea_(company)" title="Alsea (company)">Alsea</a> and Colombia's <a href="/wiki/Grupo_Nutresa" title="Grupo Nutresa">Grupo Nutresa</a> that has previously worked with Starbucks by providing coffee through Colcafe. This announcement comes after Starbucks's Farmer Support Center was established in <a href="/wiki/Manizales" title="Manizales">Manizales</a>, Colombia the previous year making Colombia an already established country by the corporation.<sup id="cite_ref-news.starbucks.com_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-news.starbucks.com-146">[146]</a></sup></p><p>On April 21, 2015, <a href="/wiki/Kesko" title="Kesko">Kesko</a>, the second largest retailer in <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a>, announced its partnership with Starbucks, with stores opened next to <a href="/wiki/K-Citymarket" title="K-Citymarket">K-Citymarket</a> hypermarkets.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> As of June 2017, 3 stores had been opened next to K-Citymarkets: In <a href="/wiki/Sello" title="Sello">Sello</a> in <a href="/wiki/Espoo" title="Espoo">Espoo</a> and in <a href="/wiki/Myyrmanni" title="Myyrmanni">Myyrmanni</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jumbo_Shopping_Centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Jumbo Shopping Centre">Jumbo</a> in <a href="/wiki/Vantaa" title="Vantaa">Vantaa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-loxcel_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loxcel-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Starbuckslomas.JPG" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Starbuckslomas.JPG/220px-Starbuckslomas.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2288" data-file-height="1592"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 153px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Starbuckslomas.JPG/220px-Starbuckslomas.JPG" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="153" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Starbuckslomas.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Starbucks in <a href="/wiki/Lomas_de_Zamora" title="Lomas de Zamora">Lomas de Zamora</a>, <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a></div></div></div>
<p>On December 18, 2015, Starbucks opened in <a href="/wiki/Almaty" title="Almaty">Almaty</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a>. On the next day, 1 more coffee shop was opened.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup></p><p>The first Starbucks store in <a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakia</a> opened in <a href="/wiki/Aupark" class="mw-redirect" title="Aupark">Aupark Shopping Center</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bratislava" title="Bratislava">Bratislava</a> on May 31, 2016,<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> with two more stores confirmed to open in Bratislava by the end of 2016.
</p><p>In February 2016, <a href="/wiki/Howard_Schultz" title="Howard Schultz">Howard Schultz</a> announced the opening of stores in <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>. The first Italian Starbucks store was inaugurated in <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a> on September 6, 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup></p><p>After Taste Holdings acquired outlet licensing for South African stores, Starbucks opened its first store in South Africa in Rosebank, Johannesburg on Thursday, April 21, 2016, and it is second in the country at the end of April in Mall of Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup></p><p>In May 2017, Starbucks announced it was commencing operations in <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a>, where the first store is to open in the resort city of <a href="/wiki/Montego_Bay" title="Montego Bay">Montego Bay</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> The company announced that its first store would be on located on the shores of the world-famous <a href="/wiki/Doctor%27s_Cave_Beach_Club" title="Doctor's Cave Beach Club">Doctor's Cave Beach</a>, offering views of the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> Starbucks Jamaica expects thereafter to roll out a further 14 locations across the island by the year 2020. The company also reaffirmed its commitment to working with local coffee farmers to "implement systems to increase productivity and yields, while also increasing compliance to international standards."<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> Starbucks Jamaica officially opened its first store on November 21, 2017, with plans to open 15 locations islandwide over a 5-year period.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> Starbucks Jamaica, recently opened its 3 stores at the <a href="/wiki/Sangster_International_Airport" title="Sangster International Airport">Sangster International Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Montego_Bay" title="Montego Bay">Montego Bay</a> and one at the <a href="/wiki/Falmouth,_Jamaica" title="Falmouth, Jamaica">Historic Falmouth Pier</a>, in Falmouth, Jamaica. Starbucks Jamaica announced its intention to open 2 stores in Jamaica's capital city, <a href="/wiki/Kingston,_Jamaica" title="Kingston, Jamaica">Kingston</a> in 2018, with plans for up to 6 stores by 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup> The first of the <a href="/wiki/Kingston,_Jamaica" title="Kingston, Jamaica">Kingston</a> stores opened on June 21, 2018. The second store is located in the heart of Kingston's central business district, New Kingston. Starbucks is also opening its first in-store location in the new flagship location for Jamaica's largest Pharmacy chain, Fontana Pharmacy, also located in Kingston; making it Starbucks's third confirmed location.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> This location will open in July 2019.
</p><p>Caribbean Coffee Baristas, franchise-holders for Starbucks's Jamaican operations are set to open new stores in the <a href="/wiki/Cayman_Islands" title="Cayman Islands">Cayman Islands</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Turks_and_Caicos" class="mw-redirect" title="Turks and Caicos">Turks and Caicos</a> Islands; up to three stores are planned for the Caymans and a yet undisclosed number for the Turks &amp; Caicos. The first of these stores will be opened by year-end of 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup></p><p>At the end of December 2017, the world's biggest Starbucks store opened at <a href="/wiki/HKRI_Taikoo_Hui" title="HKRI Taikoo Hui">HKRI Taikoo Hui</a> in <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">Shanghai</a>, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>.
</p><p>Starbucks announced the opening of stores in <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a> in late 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> The first store was opened in April 2019 at <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rajiceva_Mall&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Rajiceva Mall (page does not exist)">Rajićeva Mall</a>.
</p><p>On June 1, 2019, Starbucks opened its first coffee store in <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a> at <a href="/wiki/Valletta" title="Valletta">Valletta</a>. This will be the 80th country that will have a Starbucks outlet.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Former">Former</span></h3>
<p>In 2003, after struggling with fierce local competition, Starbucks, along with its partner <a href="/wiki/Delek" title="Delek">Delek Group of Israel</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Starbucks_Israel" title="Starbucks Israel">closed all six of its locations</a> in <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>, citing "on-going operational challenges" and a "difficult business environment."<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup></p><p>The Starbucks location in the <a href="/wiki/Forbidden_City" title="Forbidden City">former imperial palace</a> in Beijing closed in July 2007. The coffee shop had been a source of ongoing controversy since its opening in 2000 with protesters objecting that the presence of the American chain in this location "was trampling on Chinese culture."<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup></p><p>In July 2008, the company announced it was closing 600 underperforming company-owned stores and cutting U.S. expansion plans amid growing economic uncertainty.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> On July 29, 2008, Starbucks also cut almost 1,000 non-retail jobs as part of its bid to re-energize the brand and boost its profit. Of the new cuts, 550 of the positions were layoffs and the rest were unfilled jobs.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup> These closings and layoffs effectively ended the company's period of growth and expansion that began in the mid-1990s.
</p><p>Starbucks also announced in July 2008 that it would close 61 of its 84 stores in Australia in the following month.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> Nick Wailes, an expert in strategic management of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Sydney" title="University of Sydney">University of Sydney</a>, commented that "Starbucks failed to truly understand Australia's cafe culture."<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> In May 2014, Starbucks announced ongoing losses in the Australian market, which resulted in the remaining stores being sold to the Withers Group.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup></p><p>In January 2009, Starbucks announced the closure of an additional 300 underperforming stores and the elimination of 7,000 positions. CEO Howard Schultz also announced that he had received board approval to reduce his salary.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup> Altogether, from February 2008 to January 2009, Starbucks terminated an estimated 18,400 U.S. jobs and began closing 977 stores worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup></p><p>In August 2009, <a href="/wiki/Ahold" title="Ahold">Ahold</a> announced closures and rebranding for 43 of their licensed store Starbucks kiosks for their US based <a href="/wiki/Stop_%26_Shop" title="Stop &amp; Shop">Stop &amp; Shop</a> and <a href="/wiki/Giant-Landover" class="mw-redirect" title="Giant-Landover">Giant</a> supermarkets.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup></p><p>In July 2012, the company announced that they may begin closing unprofitable European stores immediately.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Unbranded_stores">Unbranded stores</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Stealth_Starbucks" title="Stealth Starbucks">Stealth Starbucks</a></div>
<p>In 2009, at least three stores in Seattle were de-branded to remove the logo and brand name, and remodel the stores as local coffee houses "inspired by Starbucks."<sup id="cite_ref-stealth_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stealth-180">[180]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-schultzbw_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-schultzbw-181">[181]</a></sup> CEO Howard Schultz says the unbranded stores are a "laboratory for Starbucks".<sup id="cite_ref-marketing_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marketing-182">[182]</a></sup> The first, 15th Avenue Coffee and Tea, opened in July 2009 on Capitol Hill. It served wine and beer and hosted live music and poetry readings.<sup id="cite_ref-seattletimes.nwsource.com_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-seattletimes.nwsource.com-183">[183]</a></sup> It has since been remodeled and reopened as a Starbucks-branded store. Another is Roy Street Coffee and Tea at 700 Broadway E., also on Capitol Hill.
